## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The nonlinearity can arise from anharmonic restoring forces, nonlinear damping, or time-dependent driving.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear damping plus restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Forced Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (forced linear oscillator)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2)**(-1) (rational restoring force with saturation)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 (velocity-cubed damping)
- Mathieu-type parametric: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (parametric excitation)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential well)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Terms like (1 - x²)*v → self-sustained oscillations with amplitude-dependent damping (limit cycles)
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system, energy conservation or dissipation governs dynamics
- Cosine/sine of time → external periodic driving force creating forced oscillation or resonance
- Position-velocity coupling x^n * v → nonlinear damping that depends on amplitude of oscillation
- Even powers of x (x²) in restoring force → broken symmetry, asymmetric oscillation about equilibrium
- Rational functions of x → bounded restoring force mimicking realistic saturation of spring stiffness
- Velocity raised to odd powers (v³) → nonlinear dissipation preserving time-reversal symmetry of damping direction
